وما يروون أنه كتب يوم الحصار إلى علي : فإن كنت مأكولاً فكن خير آكل وإلا فأدركني ولما أمزق - فلا أصل له إذ المعروف من أمر عثمان أنه كان يتحامى من الحرب ويتجوز عن ذلك حتى قال: من وضع السلاح من غلماني فهو حر. ومن كان هذا - مع من قصد الحرب من غلمانه - فعله فكيف يستعين بعلي ؟! وكيف يستنصر من هو جاد في نصره مشمر ذيله في ذلك؟! وروى عنه أنه قال : - والله ما قتلت عثمان ولا مالات في قتله - وما روي عن علي أنه قال في أمر عثمان: الله قتله وأنا معه - معناه: وأنا مع عثمان وكانت الهاء عائدة إلى عثمان دون الله تعالى، وأخبر أنه يستشهد كما استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنهما. يحققه أنه قال على المنبر : - قتلت يوم قتل الثور الأبيض - وهو مثل مشهور في العرب، أخبر بذلك أنه يستشهد كما استشهد هو، والله الموفق.
And what they narrate that he wrote during the siege to Ali: 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater; otherwise, save me before I am torn apart' – it has no basis. For the known fact about Uthman is that he used to avoid war and resolve to avoid it, to the extent that he said: 'Whoever lays down his weapon from my slaves is free.' And if he did this with those who intended war from his slaves, how could he seek help from Ali?! And how could he seek victory from one who was earnest in his support, rolling up his sleeves for that?! And it is narrated from him that he said: 'By Allah, I did not kill Uthman nor did I incline to his killing.' And what is narrated from Ali that he said regarding the matter of Uthman: 'Allah killed him and I am with him' – its meaning is: I am with Uthman, and the pronoun refers to Uthman, not to Allah Almighty. And he informed that he would be martyred just as Uthman was martyred, may Allah be pleased with them both. This is confirmed by what he said on the pulpit: 'I am killed on the day the white bull is killed' – and this is a well-known proverb among the Arabs. He informed by that that he would be martyred just as he (Uthman) was martyred. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1165

Commentary
This passage refutes two related reports. First, the claim that Uthman wrote a line of poetry to Ali during the siege saying 'If I am to be eaten, then be the best eater.' The author says this has no basis because Uthman was known to avoid war, even freeing slaves who laid down arms, so how could he ask Ali for military help? Second, the report that Ali said 'Allah killed Uthman and I am with him.' The author explains that 'with him' means with Uthman, not with Allah, and that Ali was prophesying his own martyrdom, as confirmed by his statement about the white bull, a proverb meaning he would die a martyr.

Key Terms
استشهد
الثور الأبيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people believe that Ali's statement 'Allah killed Uthman and I am with him' indicates his tacit approval or involvement in the assassination.
Correction: The author explains that 'I am with him' means 'I am with Uthman' (in martyrdom) and that Ali was prophesying his own death.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does Ali's statement 'Allah killed Uthman and I am with him' actually mean?
A) Ali was with Allah in killing Uthman.
B) Ali was with Uthman and would also be martyred.
C) Ali denied any knowledge of the killing.
D) Ali expressed regret for not helping Uthman.

Key Takeaway
Ali's statement about being with Uthman refers to his own future martyrdom, not to involvement in Uthman's death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a quote from a Companion that seems to incriminate them, do you immediately accept it at face value, or do you follow the example of this lesson by seeking a correct interpretation? What will you do differently the next time you hear such a report?
?
If you were falsely accused of a crime, could you trust that Allah would eventually vindicate you, just as Ali trusted that his statement would be correctly understood? What is one step you can take today to strengthen that trust in your own life?
?
Think of a situation where you judged someone harshly based on a single ambiguous statement. How does Ali's clarification challenge you to reconsider that judgment and to seek the full context before forming your opinion?
